 </b><p>Prayers</p>  
 <p>   1. The Lord's Prayer. </p> 
 <p>   2. The Angelical Salutation. </p> 
 <p>   3. The Apostles' Creed. </p> 
 <p>   4. The Confiteor. </p> 
 <p>   5. An Act of Faith. </p> 
 <p>   6. An Act of Hope. </p> 
 <p>   7. An Act of Love. </p> 
 <p>   8. An Act of Contrition. </p> 
 <p>   9. The Blessing before Meals. </p> 
 <p>  10.Grace after Meals.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>The Lessons of the Catechism</p>  
 <p>   1. Lesson 1 On the end of Man </p> 
 <p>   2. Lesson 2 On God and His Perfections </p> 
 <p>   3. Lesson 3 On the Unity and Trinity of God </p> 
 <p>   4. Lesson 4 On Creation </p> 
 <p>   5. Lesson 5 On Our First Parents and the Fall </p> 
 <p>   6. Lesson 6 On Sin and Its Kinds </p> 
 <p>   7. Lesson 7 On the Incarnation and Redemption </p> 
 <p>   8. Lesson 8 On Our Lord's Passion, Death, Resurrection and Ascension </p> 
 <p>   9. Lesson 9 On the Holy Gost and His Descent Upon the Apostles </p> 
 <p>  10. Lesson 10 On the Effects of the Redemption </p> 
 <p>  11. Lesson 11 On the Church </p> 
 <p>  12. Lesson 12 On the Attributes and Marks of the Church </p> 
 <p>  13. Lesson 13 On the Sacraments in General </p> 
 <p>  14. Lesson 14 On Baptism </p> 
 <p>  15. Lesson 15 On Confirmation </p> 
 <p>  16. Lesson 16 On the Gifts and Fruits of the Holy Ghost </p> 
 <p>  17. Lesson 17 On the Sacrament of Penance </p> 
 <p>  18. Lesson 18 On Contrition </p> 
 <p>  19. Lesson 19 On Confession </p> 
 <p>  20. Lesson 20 On the Manner of Making a Good Confession </p> 
 <p>  21. Lesson 21 On Indulgences </p> 
 <p>  22. Lesson 22 On the Holy Eucharist </p> 
 <p>  23. Lesson 23 On the Ends for which the Holy Eucharist was Instituted </p> 
 <p>  24. Lesson 24 On the Sacrifice of the Mass </p> 
 <p>  25. Lesson 25 On Extreme Unction and Holy Orders </p> 
 <p>  26. Lesson 26 On Matrimony </p> 
 <p>  27. Lesson 27 On the Sacramentals </p> 
 <p>  28. Lesson 28 On Prayer </p> 
 <p>  29. Lesson 29 On the Commandments of God </p> 
 <p>  30. Lesson 30 On the First Commandment </p> 
 <p>  31. Lesson 31 The First Commandment -- On the Honor and Invocation of the Saints </p> 
 <p>  32. Lesson 32 From the Second to the Fourth Commandment </p> 
 <p>  33. Lesson 33 From the Fourth to the Seventh Commandment </p> 
 <p>  34. Lesson 34 From the Seventh to the Tenth Commandment </p> 
 <p>  35. Lesson 35 On the First and Second Commandments of the Church </p> 
 <p>  36. Lesson 36 On the Third, Fourth, Fifth and Sixth Commandments of the Church </p> 
 <p>  37. Lesson 37 On the Last Judgment and Resurrection, Hell, Purgatory and Heaven</p>  
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Prayers:</p>  <b>
 </b><p>The Lord's Prayer.</p>  
 <p>Our Father, who art in heaven, hallowed be Thy name. Thy kingdom come; Thy will be</p> 
 <p>done on earth as it is in heaven. Give us this day our daily bread; and forgive us our</p> 
 <p>trespasses as we forgive those who trespass against us; and lead us not into temptation,</p> 
 <p>but deliver us from evil. Amen. </p>  <b>
 </b><p>The Angelical Salutation.</p>  
 <p>Hail Mary, full of grace! the Lord is with thee: blessed art thou amongst women, and</p> 
 <p>blessed is the fruit of thy womb, Jesus. Holy Mary, Mother of God, pray for us sinners,</p> 
 <p>now and at the hour of our death. Amen. </p>  <b>
 </b><p>The Apostles' Creed.</p>  
 <p>I believe in God, the Father Almighty, Creator of heaven and earth; and in Jesus Christ,</p> 
 <p>His only Son, our Lord; who was conceived by the Holy Ghost, born of the Virgin Mary,</p> 
 <p>suffered under Pontius Pilate, was crucified; died, and was buried. He descended into</p> 
 <p>hell; the third day He arose again from the dead; He ascended into heaven, sitteth at the</p> 
 <p>right hand of God, the Father Almighty; from thence He shall come to judge the living and</p> 
 <p>the dead. I believe in the Holy Ghost the Holy Catholic Church, the communion of Saints,</p> 
 <p>the forgiveness of sins, the resurrection of the body, and the life everlasting. Amen. </p>  <b>
 </b><p>The Confiteor.</p>  
 <p>I confess to Almighty God, to blessed Mary, ever Virgin, to blessed Michael the</p> 
 <p>Archangel, to blessed John the Baptist, to the holy Apostles Peter and Paul, and to all the</p> 
 <p>Saints, that I have sinned exceedingly in thought, word and deed, through, my fault,</p> 
 <p>through my fault, through my most grievous fault. Therefore, I beseech blessed Mary, ever</p> 
 <p>Virgin, blessed Michael the Archangel, blessed John the Baptist, the holy Apostles Peter</p> 
 <p>and Paul, and all the Saints, to pray to the Lord our God for me. </p>  
 <p>May the Almighty God have mercy on me, and forgive me my sins, and bring me to</p> 
 <p>everlasting life. Amen. </p>  
 <p>May the Almighty and merciful Lord grant me pardon, absolution, and remission of all my</p> 
 <p>sins. Amen. </p>  <b>
 </b><p>An Act of Faith.</p>  
 <p>0 my God! I firmly believe that Thou art one God in three Divine persons, Father, Son,</p> 
 <p>and Holy Ghost; I believe that Thy Divine Son became man, and died for our sins, and</p> 
 <p>that he will come to, judge the living and the dead. I believe these and all the truths which</p> 
 <p>the Holy Catholic Church teaches, because Thou hast revealed them, who canst neither</p> 
 <p>deceive nor be deceived </p>  <b>
 </b><p>An Act of Hope.</p>  
 <p>0 my God! relying on Thy infinite goodness and promises, I hope to obtain pardon of my</p> 
 <p>sins, the help of Thy grace, and life everlasting, through the merits of Jesus Christ, my</p> 
 <p>Lord and Redeemer. </p>  <b>
 </b><p>An Act of Love.</p>  
 <p>0 my God! I love Thee above all things, with my whole heart and soul, because Thou art</p> 
 <p>all-good and worthy of all love. I love my neighbor as myself for the love of Thee. I</p> 
 <p>forgive all who have injured me, and ask pardon of all whom I have injured. </p>  <b>
 </b><p>An Act of Contrition.</p>  
 <p>0 my God! I am heartily sorry for having offended Thee, and I detest all my sins, because</p> 
 <p>I dread the loss of heaven and the pains of hell; but most of all because they offend Thee,</p> 
 <p>my God, who art all-good and deserving of all my love. I firmly resolve, with the help of</p> 
 <p>Thy grace, to confess my sins, to do penance, and to amend my life. </p>  <b>
 </b><p>The Blessing before Meals.</p>  
 <p> Bless us, 0 Lord! and these Thy gifts, which we are about to receive from Thy bounty,</p> 
 <p>through Christ our Lord. Amen. </p>  <b>
 </b><p>Grace after Meals.</p>  
 <p> We give Thee thanks for all Thy benefits, 0 Almighty God, who livest and reignest for</p> 
 <p>ever; and may the souls of the faithful departed, through the mercy of God, rest in peace.</p> 
 <p>Amen. </p>  
 <p>The Manner in which a Lay Person is to Baptize in Case of Necessity:</p>  
 <p>Pour common water on the head or face of the person to be baptized say while pouring it:</p>  
 <p>"I baptize thee in the name of the Father, and of the Son, and of the Holy Ghost." </p>  
 <p>N.B. Any person of either sex who has reached the use of reason can baptize in case of</p> 
 <p>necessity. </p>  
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>LESSON FIRST: On the End of Man. </p>  <b>
 </b><p>Q. 126. What do we mean by the "end of man"? </p> 
 <p>A. By the "end of man" we mean the purpose for which he was created: namely, to know,</p> 
 <p>love, and serve God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 127. How do you know that man was created for God alone? </p> 
 <p>A. I know that man was created for God alone because everything in the world was</p> 
 <p>created for something more perfect than itself: but there is nothing in the world more</p> 
 <p>perfect than man; therefore, he was created for something outside this world, and since he</p> 
 <p>was not created for the Angels, he must have been created for God.</p>  <b>
 </b><p>Q. 128. In what respect are all men equal? </p> 
 <p>A. All men are equal in whatever is necessary for their nature and end. They are all</p> 
 <p>composed of a body and soul; they are all created to the image and likeness of God; they</p> 
 <p>are all gifted with understanding and free will; and they have all been created for the same</p> 
 <p>end -- God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 129. Do not men differ in many things? </p> 
 <p>A. Men differ in many things, such as learning, wealth, power, etc.; but these things belong</p> 
 <p>to the world and not man's nature. He came into this world without them and he will leave</p> 
 <p>it without them. Only the consequences of good or evil done in this world will accompany</p> 
 <p>men to the next.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 130. Who made the world? </p> 
 <p>A. God made the world.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 131. What does "world" mean in this question? </p> 
 <p>A. In this question "world" means the universe; that is, the whole creation; all that we now</p> 
 <p>see or may hereafter see.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 132. Who is God? </p> 
 <p>A. God is the Creator of heaven and earth, and of all things.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 133. What is man? </p> 
 <p>A. Man is a creature composed of body and soul, and made to the image and likeness of</p> 
 <p>God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 134. Does "man" in the Catechism mean all human beings? </p> 
 <p>A. "Man" in the Catechism means all human beings, either men or women, boys, girls, or</p> 
 <p>children.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 135. What is a creature? </p> 
 <p>A. A creature is anything created, whether it has life or not; body or no body. Every</p> 
 <p>being, person, or thing except God Himself may be called a creature.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 136. Is this likeness in the body or in the soul? </p> 
 <p>A. This likeness is chiefly in the soul.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 137. How is the soul like to God?</p> 
 <p>A. The soul is like to God because it is a spirit that will never die, and has understanding</p> 
 <p>and free will.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 138. Is every invisible thing a spirit? </p> 
 <p>A. Every spirit is invisible -- which means can not be seen; but every invisible thing is not a</p> 
 <p>spirit. The wind is invisible, and it is not a spirit.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 139. Has a spirit any other quality? </p> 
 <p>A. A spirit is also indivisible; that is, it can not be divided into parts, as we divide material</p> 
 <p>things.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 140. What do the words "will never die" mean? </p> 
 <p>A. By the words "will never die" we mean that the soul, when once created, will never</p> 
 <p>cease to exist, whatever be its condition in the next world. Hence we say the soul is</p> 
 <p>immortal or gifted with immortality.</p>  <b>
 </b><p>Q. 141. Why then do we say a soul is dead while in a state of mortal sin? </p> 
 <p>A. We say a soul is dead while in a state of mortal sin, because in that state it is as</p> 
 <p>helpless as a dead body, and can merit nothing for itself.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 142. What does our "understanding" mean? </p> 
 <p>A. Our "understanding" means the "gift of reason," by which man is distinguished from all</p> 
 <p>other animals, and by which he is enabled to think and thus acquire knowledge and</p> 
 <p>regulate his actions.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 143. Can we learn all truths by our reason alone? </p> 
 <p>A. We can not learn all truths by our reason alone, for some truths are beyond the power</p> 
 <p>of our reason and must be taught to us by God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 144. What do we call the truths God teaches us? </p> 
 <p>A. Taken together, we call the truths God teaches us revelation, and we call the manner</p> 
 <p>by which He teaches them also revelation.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 145. What is "Free Will"? </p> 
 <p>A. "Free Will" is that gift of God by which we are enabled to choose between one thing</p> 
 <p>and another; and to do good or evil in spite of reward or punishment.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 146. Have brute animals "understanding" and "free will"? </p> 
 <p>A. Brute animals have not "understanding" and "free will." They have not "understanding"</p> 
 <p>because they never change their habits or better their condition. They have not "free will"</p> 
 <p>because they never show it in their actions.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 147. What gift in animals supplies the place of reason? </p> 
 <p>A. In animals the gift of "instinct" supplies the place of reason in guiding their actions.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 148. What is instinct? </p> 
 <p>A. "Instinct" is a gift by which all animals are impelled to follow the laws and habits that</p> 
 <p>God has given to their nature.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 149. Have men as well as brutes "instinct"? </p> 
 <p>A. Men have "instinct," and they show it when placed in sudden danger, when they have</p> 
 <p>not time to use their reason. A falling man instantly grasps for something to support him.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 150. Why did God make you? </p> 
 <p>A. God made me to know Him, to love Him, and to serve Him in this world, and to be</p> 
 <p>happy with Him forever in the next.</p>  <b>
 </b><p>Q. 151. Why is it necessary to know God? </p> 
 <p>A. It is necessary to know God because without knowing Him we cannot love Him; and</p> 
 <p>without loving Him we cannot be saved. We should know Him because He is infinitely</p> 
 <p>true; love Him because He is infinitely beautiful; and serve Him because He is infinitely</p> 
 <p>good.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 152. Of which must we take more care, our soul or our body? </p> 
 <p>A. We must take more care of our soul than of our body.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 153. Why must we take more care of our soul than of our body? </p> 
 <p>A. We must take more care of our soul than of our body, because in losing our soul we</p> 
 <p>lose God and everlasting happiness.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 154. What must we do to save our souls? </p>  
 <p>A. To save our souls, we must worship God by faith, hope, and charity; that is, we must</p> 
 <p>believe in Him, hope in Him, and love Him with all our heart.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 155. What does "worship" mean? </p> 
 <p>A. "Worship" means to give divine honor by acts such as the offering of prayer or</p> 
 <p>sacrifice.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 156. How shall we know the things which we are to believe? </p> 
 <p>A. We shall know the things which we are to believe from the Catholic Church, through</p> 
 <p>which God speaks to us.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 157. What do we mean by the "Church, through which God speaks to us"? </p> 
 <p>A. By the "Church, through which God speaks to us," we mean the "teaching Church";</p> 
 <p>that is, the Pope, Bishops, and priests, whose duty it is to instruct us in the truths and</p> 
 <p>practices of our religion.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 158. Where shall we find the chief truths which the Church teaches? </p> 
 <p>A. We shall find the chief truths which the Church teaches in the Apostles' Creed.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 159. If we shall find only the "chief truths" in the Apostles' Creed, where shall</p> 
 <p>we find the remaining truths? </p> 
 <p>A. We shall find the remaining truths of our Faith in the religious writings and preachings</p> 
 <p>that have been sanctioned by the authority of the Church.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 160. Name some sacred truths not mentioned in the Apostles' Creed. </p> 
 <p>A. In the Apostles' Creed there is no mention of the Real Presence of Our Lord in the</p> 
 <p>Holy Eucharist, nor of the Infallibility of the Pope, nor of the Immaculate Conception of</p> 
 <p>the Blessed Virgin Mary, nor of some other truths that we are bound to believe.</p>  <b>
 </b><p>Q. 161. Say the Apostles' Creed. </p>  
 <p>A. I believe in God, the Father Almighty, Creator of heaven and earth; and in Jesus</p> 
 <p>Christ, His only Son, our Lord; who was conceived by the Holy Ghost, born of the Virgin</p> 
 <p>Mary, suffered under Pontius Pilate, was crucified; died, and was buried. He descended</p> 
 <p>into hell: the third day He arose again from the dead: He ascended into heaven, sitteth at</p> 
 <p>the right hand of God, the Father Almighty: from thence He shall come to judge the living</p> 
 <p>and the dead. I believe in the Holy Ghost, the Holy Catholic Church, the communion of</p> 
 <p>Saints, the forgiveness of sins, the resurrection of the body, and the life everlasting. Amen.</p>  
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>LESSON SECOND: On God and His Perfections </p>  <b>
 </b><p>Q. 162. What is a perfection? </p> 
 <p>A. A perfection is any good quality a thing should have. A thing is perfect when it has all the good qualities it should have.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 163. What is God? </p> 
 <p>A. God is a spirit infinitely perfect.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 164. What do we mean when we say God is "infinitely perfect"? </p> 
 <p>A. When we say God is "infinitely perfect" we mean there is no limit or bounds to His perfection; for He possesses all good qualities in the highest possible degree and He alone is "infinitely perfect."</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 165. Had God a beginning? </p> 
 <p>A. God had no beginning; He always was and He always will be.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 166. Where is God? </p> 
 <p>A. God is everywhere.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 167. How is God everywhere? </p> 
 <p>A. God is everywhere whole and entire as He is in any one place. This is true and we must believe it, though we</p> 
 <p>cannot understand it.</p> <b> 
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 168. If God is everywhere, why do we not see Him? </p> 
 <p>A. We do not see God, because He is a pure spirit and cannot be seen with bodily eyes.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 169. Why do we call God a "pure spirit'? </p> 
 <p>A. We call God a pure spirit because He has no body. Our soul is a spirit, but not a "pure" spirit, because it was</p> 
 <p>created for union with our body.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 170. Why can we not see God with the eyes of our body? </p> 
 <p>A. We cannot see God with the eyes of our body because they are created to see only material things, and God is</p> 
 <p>not material but spiritual.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q 171. Does God see us? </p> 
 <p>A. God sees us and watches over us.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 172. Is it necessary for God to watch over us? </p> 
 <p>A. It is necessary for God to watch over us, for without His constant care we could not exist.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 173. Does God know all things? </p> 
 <p>A. God knows all things, even our most secret thoughts, words, and actions.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 174. Can God do all things? </p> 
 <p>A. God can do all things, and nothing is hard or impossible to Him.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 175. When is a thing said to be "impossible"? </p> 
 <p>A. A thing is said to be "impossible" when it cannot be done. Many things that are impossible for creatures are</p> 
 <p>possible for God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 176. Is God just, holy, and merciful? </p> 
 <p>A. God is all just, all holy, all merciful, as He is infinitely perfect.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 177. Why must God be "just" as well as "merciful"? </p> 
 <p>A. God must be just as well as merciful because He must fulfill His promise to punish those who merit punishment, and because He cannot be infinite in one perfection without being infinite in all.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 178. Into what sins will the forgetfulness of God's justice lead us? </p> 
 <p>A. The forgetfulness of God's justice will lead us into sins of presumption.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q 179. Into what sins will the forgetfulness of God's mercy lead us? </p> 
 <p>A. The forgetfulness of God's mercy will lead us into sins of despair.</p>  
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>LESSON THIRD: On the Unity and Trinity of God </p>  <b>
 </b><p>Q. 180. What does "unity," and what does "trinity" mean? </p> 
 <p>A. "Unity" means being one, and "trinity" means three-fold or three in one.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 181. Can we find an example to fully illustrate the mystery of the Blessed Trinity? </p> 
 <p>A. We cannot find an example to fully illustrate the mystery of the Blessed Trinity, because the mysteries of our</p> 
 <p>holy religion are beyond comparison.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 182. Is there but one God? </p> 
 <p>A. Yes; there is but one God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 183. Why can there be but one God? </p> 
 <p>A. There can be but one God because God, being supreme and infinite, cannot have an equal.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 184. What does "supreme" mean? </p> 
 <p>A. "Supreme" means the highest in authority; also the most excellent or greatest possible in anything. Thus in all</p> 
 <p>things God is supreme, and in the Church the Pope is supreme.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 185. When are two persons said to be equal? </p> 
 <p>A. Two persons are said to be equal when one is in no way greater than or inferior to the other.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 186. How many persons are there in God? </p> 
 <p>A. In God there are three Divine persons, really distinct, and equal in all things --the Father, the Son, and the Holy</p> 
 <p>Ghost.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 187. What do "divine" and "distinct" mean? </p> 
 <p>A. "Divine" means pertaining to God, and "distinct" means separate; that is, not confounded or mixed with any</p> 
 <p>other thing.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 188. Is the Father God? </p> 
 <p>A. The Father is God and the first Person of the Blessed Trinity.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 189. Is the Son God? </p> 
 <p>A. The Son is God and the second Person of the Blessed Trinity.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 190. Is the Holy Ghost God? </p> 
 <p>A. The Holy Ghost is God and the third Person of the Blessed Trinity.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 191. Do "first," "second," and "third" with regard to the persons of the Blessed Trinity mean that one</p> 
 <p>person existed before the other or that one is greater than the other? </p> 
 <p>A. "First," "second," and "third" with regard to the persons of the Blessed Trinity do not mean that one person was before the other or that one is greater than the other; for all the persons of the Trinity are eternal and equal in every respect. These numbers are used to mark the distinction between the persons, and they show the order in which the one proceeded from the other.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 192. What do you mean by the Blessed Trinity? </p> 
 <p>A. By the Blessed Trinity I mean one God in three Divine Persons.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 193. Are the three Divine Persons equal in all things? </p> 
 <p>A. The three Divine Persons are equal in all things.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 194. Are the three Divine Persons one and the same God? </p> 
 <p>A. The three Divine Persons are one and the same God, having one and the same Divine nature and substance.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 195. What do we mean by the "nature" and "substance" of a thing? </p> 
 <p>A. By the "nature" of a thing we mean the combination of all the qualities that make the thing what it is. By the</p> 
 <p>"substance" of a thing we mean the part that never changes, and which cannot be changed without destroying the</p> 
 <p>nature of the thing.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 196. Can we fully understand how the three Divine Persons are one and the same God? </p> 
 <p>A. We cannot fully understand how the three Divine Persons are one and the same God, because this is a mystery.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 197. What is a mystery? </p> 
 <p>A. A mystery is a truth which we cannot fully understand.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 198. Is every truth which we cannot understand a mystery? </p> 
 <p>A. Every truth which we cannot understand is not a mystery; but every revealed truth which no one can understand is a mystery.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 199. Should we believe truths which we cannot understand? </p> 
 <p>A. We should and often do believe truths which we cannot understand when we have proof of their existence.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 200. Give an example of truths which all believe, though many do not understand them. </p> 
 <p>A. All believe that the earth is round and moving, though many do not understand it. All believe that a seed planted in the ground will produce a flower or tree often with more than a thousand other seeds equal to itself, though many cannot understand how this is done.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 201. Why must a divine religion have mysteries? </p> 
 <p>A. A divine religion must have mysteries because it must have supernatural truths and God Himself must teach</p> 
 <p>them. A religion that has only natural truths, such as man can know by reason alone, fully understand and teach, is only a human religion.</p>  <b>
 </b><p>Q. 202. Why does God require us to believe mysteries? </p> 
 <p>A. God requires us to believe mysteries that we may submit our understanding to Him.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 203. By what form of prayer do we praise the Holy Trinity? </p> 
 <p>A. We praise the Holy Trinity by a form of prayer called the Doxology, which has come down to us almost from</p> 
 <p>the time of the Apostles.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 204. Say the Doxology. </p> 
 <p>A. The Doxology is: "Glory be to the Father, and to the Son, and to the Holy Ghost. As it was in the beginning, is</p> 
 <p>now, and ever shall be, world without end. Amen."</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 205. Is there any other form of the Doxology? </p> 
 <p>A. There is another form of the Doxology, which is said in the celebration of the Mass. It is called the "Gloria in</p> 
 <p>excelsis" or "Glory be to God on high," etc., the words sung by the Angels at the birth of Our Lord.</p>  
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>LESSON FOURTH: On Creation </p>  <b>
 </b><p>Q. 206. What is the difference between making and creating? </p> 
 <p>A. "Making" means bringing forth or forming out of some material already existing, as workmen do. "Creating"</p> 
 <p>means bringing forth out of nothing, as God alone can do.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 207. Has everything that exists been created? </p> 
 <p>A. Everything that exists except God Himself has been created.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 208. Who created heaven and earth, and all things? </p> 
 <p>A. God created heaven and earth, and all things.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 209. From what do we learn that God created heaven and earth and all things? </p> 
 <p>A. We learn that God created heaven and earth and all things from the Bible or Holy Scripture, in which the</p> 
 <p>account of the Creation is given.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 210. Why did God create all things? </p> 
 <p>A. God created all things for His own glory and for their or our good.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 211. Did God leave all things to themselves after He had created them? </p> 
 <p>A. God did not leave all things to themselves after He had created them; He continues to preserve and govern</p> 
 <p>them.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 212. What do we call the care by which God preserves and governs the world and all it contains? </p> 
 <p>A. We call the care by which God preserves and governs the world and all it contains His providence.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 213. How did God create heaven and earth? </p> 
 <p>A. God created heaven and earth from nothing by His word only; that is, by a single act of His all-powerful will.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 214. Which are the chief creatures of God? </p> 
 <p>A. The chief creatures of God are angels and men.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 215. How may God's creatures on earth be divided? </p> 
 <p>A. God's creatures on earth may be divided into four classes:</p> 
 <p>   1.(1) Things that exist, as air; </p> 
 <p>   2.(2) Things that exist, grow and live, as plants and trees; </p> 
 <p>   3.(3) Things that exist, grow, live and feel, as animals; </p> 
 <p>   4.(4) Things that exist, grow, live, feel and understand, as man.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 216. What are angels? </p> 
 <p>A. Angels are pure spirits without a body, created to adore and enjoy God in heaven.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 217. If Angels have no bodies, how could they appear? </p> 
 <p>A. Angels could appear by taking bodies to render themselves visible for a time; just as the Holy Ghost took the</p> 
 <p>form of a dove and the devil took the form of a serpent.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 218. Name some persons to whom Angels appeared. </p> 
 <p>A. Angels appeared to the Blessed Virgin and St. Joseph; also to Abraham, Lot, Jacob, Tobias and others.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 219. Were the angels created for any other purpose? </p> 
 <p>A. The angels were also created to assist before the throne of God and to minister unto Him; they have often been</p> 
 <p>sent as messengers from God to man; and are also appointed our guardians.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 220. Are all the Angels equal in dignity? </p> 
 <p>A. All the Angels are not equal in dignity. There are nine choirs or classes mentioned in the Holy Scripture. The</p> 
 <p>highest are called Seraphim and the lowest simply Angels. The Archangels are one class higher than ordinary Angels.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 221. Mention some Archangels and tell what they did. </p> 
 <p>A. The Archangel Michael drove Satan out of heaven; the Archangel Gabriel announced to the Blessed Virgin that she was to become the Mother of God. The Archangel Raphael guided and protected Tobias.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 222. Were Angels ever sent to punish men? </p> 
 <p>A. Angels were sometimes sent to punish men. An Angel killed 185,000 men in the army of a wicked king who</p> 
 <p>had blasphemed God; an Angel also slew the first-born in the families of the Egyptians who had persecuted God's</p> 
 <p>people.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 223. What do our guardian Angels do for us? </p> 
 <p>A. Our guardian Angels pray for us, protect and guide us, and offer our prayers, good works and desires to God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 224. How do we know that Angels offer our prayers and good works to God? </p> 
 <p>A. We know that Angels offer our prayers and good works to God because it is so stated in Holy Scripture, and</p> 
 <p>Holy Scripture is the Word of God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 225. Why did God appoint guardian Angels if He watches over us Himself? </p> 
 <p>A. God appointed guardian Angels to secure for us their help and prayers, and also to show His great love for us</p> 
 <p>in giving us these special servants and faithful friends.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 226. Were the angels, as God created them, good and happy? </p> 
 <p>A. The angels, as God created them, were good and happy.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 227. Did all the angels remain good and happy? </p> 
 <p>A. All the angels did not remain good and happy; many of them sinned and were cast into hell, and these are called devils or bad angels.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 228. Do we know the number of good and bad Angels? </p> 
 <p>A. We do not know the number of the good or bad Angels, but we know it is very great.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 229. What was the devil's name before he fell, and why was he cast out of heaven? </p> 
 <p>A. Before he fell, Satan, or the devil, was called Lucifer, or light-bearer, a name which indicates great beauty. He</p> 
 <p>was cast out of heaven because through pride he rebelled against God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 230. How do the bad Angels act toward us? </p> 
 <p>A. The bad Angels try by every means to lead us into sin. The efforts they make are called temptations of the devil.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 231. Why does the devil tempt us? </p> 
 <p>A. The devil tempts us because he hates goodness, and does not wish us to enjoy the happiness which he himself</p> 
 <p>has lost.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 232. Can we by our own power overcome the temptations of the devil? </p> 
 <p>A. We cannot by our own power overcome the temptations of the devil, because the devil is wiser than we are;</p> 
 <p>for, being an Angel, he is more intelligent, and he did not lose his intelligence by falling into sin any more than we do now. Therefore, to overcome his temptations we need the help of God.</p>  
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>LESSON FIFTH: On our First Parents and the Fall </p>  <b>
 </b><p>Q. 233. Who were the first man and woman? </p> 
 <p>A. The first man and woman were Adam and Eve.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 234. Are there any persons in the world who are not the descendants of Adam and Eve? </p> 
 <p>A. There are no persons in the world now, and there never have been any, who are not the descendants of Adam</p> 
 <p>and Eve, because the whole human race had but one origin.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 235. Do not the differences in color, figure, etc., which we find in distinct races indicate a difference in</p> 
 <p>first parents? </p> 
 <p>A. The differences in color, figure, etc., which we find in distinct races do not indicate a difference in first parents, for these differences have been brought about in the lapse of time by other causes, such as climate, habits, etc.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 236. Were Adam and Eve innocent and holy when they came from the hand of God? </p> 
 <p>A. Adam and Eve were innocent and holy when they came from the hand of God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 237. What do we mean by saying Adam and Eve "were innocent" when they came from the hand of</p> 
 <p>God? </p> 
 <p>A. When we say Adam and Eve "were innocent" when they came from the hand of God we mean they were in the</p> 
 <p>state of original justice; that is, they were gifted with every virtue and free from every sin.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 238. How was Adam's body formed? </p> 
 <p>A. God formed Adam's body out of the clay of the earth and then breathed into it a living soul.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 239. How was Eve's body formed? </p> 
 <p>A. Eve's body was formed from a rib taken from Adam's side during a deep sleep which God caused to come</p> 
 <p>upon him.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 240. Why did God make Eve from one of Adam's ribs? </p> 
 <p>A. God made Eve from one of Adam's ribs to show the close relationship existing between husband and wife in</p> 
 <p>their marriage union which God then instituted.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 241. Could man's body be developed from the body of an inferior animal? </p> 
 <p>A. Man's body could be developed from the body of an inferior animal if God so willed; but science does not</p> 
 <p>prove that man's body was thus formed, while revelation teaches that it was formed directly by God from the clay</p> 
 <p>of the earth.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 242. Could man's soul and intelligence be formed by the development of animal life and instinct? </p> 
 <p>A. Man's soul could not be formed by the development of animal instinct; for, being entirely spiritual, it must be</p> 
 <p>created by God, and it is united to the body as soon as the body is prepared to receive it.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 243. Did God give any command to Adam and Eve? </p> 
 <p>A. To try their obedience, God commanded Adam and Eve not to eat of a certain fruit which grew in the garden of Paradise.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 244. What was the Garden of Paradise? </p> 
 <p>A. The Garden of Paradise was a large and beautiful place prepared for man's habitation upon earth. It was</p> 
 <p>supplied with every species of plant and animal and with everything that could contribute to man's happiness.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 245. Where was the Garden of Paradise situated? </p> 
 <p>A. The exact place in which the Garden of Paradise -- called also the Garden of Eden -- was situated is not</p> 
 <p>known, for the deluge may have so changed the surface of the earth that old landmarks were wiped out. It was</p> 
 <p>probably some place in Asia, not far from the river Euphrates.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 246. What was the tree bearing the forbidden fruit called? </p> 
 <p>A. The tree bearing the forbidden fruit was called "the tree of knowledge of good and evil."</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 247. Do we know the name of any other tree in the garden? </p> 
 <p>A. We know the name of another tree in the Garden called the "tree of life." Its fruit kept the bodies of our first</p> 
 <p>parents in a state of perfect health.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 248. Which were the chief blessings intended for Adam and Eve had they remained faithful to God? </p> 
 <p>A. The chief blessings intended for Adam and Eve, had they remained faithful to God, were a constant state of</p> 
 <p>happiness in this life and everlasting glory in the next.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 249. Did Adam and Eve remain faithful to God? </p> 
 <p>A. Adam and Eve did not remain faithful to God, but broke His command by eating the forbidden fruit.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 250. Who was the first to disobey God? </p> 
 <p>A. Eve was the first to disobey God, and she induced Adam to do likewise.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 251. How was Eve tempted to sin? </p> 
 <p>A. Eve was tempted to sin by the devil, who came in the form of a serpent and persuaded her to break God's</p> 
 <p>command.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 252. Which were the chief causes that led Eve into sin? </p> 
 <p>A. The chief causes that led Eve into sin were:</p>  
 <p>   1.(1) She went into the danger of sinning by admiring what was forbidden, instead of avoiding it. </p> 
 <p>   2.(2) She did not fly from the temptation at once, but debated about yielding to it.</p>  
 <p>Similar conduct on our part will lead us also into sin.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 253. What befell Adam and Eve on account of their sin? </p> 
 <p>A. Adam and Eve, on account of their sin, lost innocence and holiness, and were doomed to sickness and death.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 254. What other evils befell Adam and Eve on account of their sin? </p> 
 <p>A. Many other evils befell Adam and Eve on account of their sin. They were driven out of Paradise and</p> 
 <p>condemned to toil. God also ordained that henceforth the earth should yield no crops without cultivation, and that</p> 
 <p>the beasts, man's former friends, should become his savage enemies.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 255. Were we to remain in the Garden of Paradise forever if Adam had not sinned? </p> 
 <p>A. We were not to remain in the Garden of Paradise forever even if Adam had not sinned, but after passing</p> 
 <p>through the years of our probation or trial upon earth we were to be taken, body and soul, into heaven without</p> 
 <p>suffering death.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 256. What evil befell us on account of the disobedience of our first parents? </p> 
 <p>A. On account of the disobedience of our first parents, we all share in their sin and punishment, as we should have</p> 
 <p>shared in their happiness if they had remained faithful.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 257. Is it not unjust to punish us for the sin of our first parents? </p> 
 <p>A. It is not unjust to punish us for the sin of our first parents, because their punishment consisted in being deprived of a free gift of God; that is, of the gift of original justice to which they had no strict right and which they willfully forfeited by their act of disobedience.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 258. But how did the loss of the gift of original justice leave our first parents and us in mortal sin? </p> 
 <p>A. The loss of the gift of original justice left our first parents and us in mortal sin because it deprived them of the</p> 
 <p>Grace of God, and to be without this gift of Grace which they should have had was to be in mortal sin. As all their</p> 
 <p>children are deprived of the same gift, they, too, come into the world in a state of mortal sin.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 259. What other effects followed from the sin of our first parents? </p> 
 <p>A. Our nature was corrupted by the sin of our first parents, which darkened our understanding, weakened our will,</p> 
 <p>and left in us a strong inclination to evil.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 260. What do we mean by "our nature was corrupted"? </p> 
 <p>A. When we say "our nature was corrupted" we mean that our whole being, body and soul, was injured in all its</p> 
 <p>parts and powers.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 261. Why do we say our understanding was darkened? </p> 
 <p>A. We say our understanding was darkened because even with much learning we have not the clear knowledge,</p> 
 <p>quick perception and retentive memory that Adam had before his fall from grace.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 262. Why do we say our will was weakened? </p> 
 <p>A. We say our will was weakened to show that our free will was not entirely taken away by Adam's sin, and that</p> 
 <p>we have it still in our power to use our free will in doing good or evil.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 263. In what does the strong inclination to evil that is left in us consist? </p> 
 <p>A. This strong inclination to evil that is left in us consists in the continual efforts our senses and appetites make to</p> 
 <p>lead our souls into sin. The body is inclined to rebel against the soul, and the soul itself to rebel against God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 264. What is this strong inclination to evil called, and why did God permit it to remain in us? </p> 
 <p>A. This strong inclination to evil is called concupiscence, and God permits it to remain in us that by His grace we</p> 
 <p>may resist it and thus increase our merits.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 265. What is the sin called which we inherit from our first parents? </p> 
 <p>A. The sin which we inherit from our first parents is called original sin.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 266. Why is this sin called original? </p> 
 <p>A. This sin is called original because it comes down to us from our first parents, and we are brought into the world with its guilt on our soul.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 267. Does this corruption of our nature remain in us after original sin is forgiven? </p> 
 <p>A. This corruption of our nature and other punishments remain in us after original sin is forgiven.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 268. Was any one ever preserved from original sin? </p> 
 <p>A. The Blessed Virgin Mary, through the merits of her Divine Son, was preserved free from the guilt of original sin, and this privilege is called her Immaculate Conception.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 269. Why was the Blessed Virgin preserved from original sin? </p> 
 <p>A. The Blessed Virgin was preserved from original sin because it would not be consistent with the dignity of the</p> 
 <p>Son of God to have His Mother, even for an instant, in the power of the devil and an enemy of God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 270. How could the Blessed Virgin be preserved from sin by her Divine Son, before her Son was born?</p> 
 <p>A. The Blessed Virgin could be preserved from sin by her Divine Son before He was born as man, for He always</p> 
 <p>existed as God and foresaw His own future merits and the dignity of His Mother. He therefore by His future merits provided for her privilege of exemption from original sin.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 271. What does the "Immaculate Conception" mean? </p> 
 <p>A. The Immaculate Conception means the Blessed Virgin's own exclusive privilege of coming into existence,</p> 
 <p>through the merits of Jesus Christ, without the stain of original sin. It does not mean, therefore, her sinless life,</p> 
 <p>perpetual virginity or the miraculous conception of Our Divine Lord by the power of the Holy Ghost.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 272. What has always been the belief of the Church concerning this truth? </p> 
 <p>A. The Church has always believed in the Immaculate Conception of the Blessed Virgin and to place this truth</p> 
 <p>beyond doubt has declared it an Article of Faith.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 273. To what should the thoughts of the Immaculate Conception lead us? </p> 
 <p>A. The thoughts of the Immaculate Conception should lead us to a great love of purity and to a desire of imitating</p> 
 <p>the Blessed Virgin in the practice of that holy virtue.</p>  
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>LESSON SIXTH: On Sin and Its Kinds  ON SIN AND ITS KINDS. </p>  <b>
 </b><p>Q. 274. How is sin divided? </p>  
 <p>A. </p>  
 <p>   1.(1) Sin is divided into the sin we inherit called original sin, and the sin we commit ourselves, called actual sin.</p> 
 <p>   2.(2) Actual sin is sub-divided into greater sins, called mortal, and lesser sins, called venial.</p>  <b>
 </b><p>Q. 275. In how many ways may actual sin be committed? </p> 
 <p>A. Actual sin may be committed in two ways: namely, by willfully doing things forbidden, or by willfully neglecting things commanded.</p>  <b>
 </b><p>Q. 276. What is our sin called when we neglect things commanded? </p> 
 <p>A. When we neglect things commanded our sin is called a sin of omission. Such sins as willfully neglecting to hear Mass on Sundays, or neglecting to go to Confession at least once a year, are sins of omission.</p>  <b>
 </b><p>Q. 277. Is original sin the only kind of sin? </p> 
 <p>A. Original sin is not the only kind of sin; there is another kind of sin, which we commit ourselves, called actual sin.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 278. What is actual sin? </p> 
 <p>A. Actual sin is any willful thought, word, deed, or omission contrary to the law of God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 279. How many kinds of actual sin are there? </p> 
 <p>A. There are two kinds of actual sin -- mortal and venial.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 280. What is mortal sin? </p> 
 <p>A. Mortal sin is a grievous offense against the law of God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 281. Why is this sin called mortal? </p> 
 <p>A. This sin is called mortal because it deprives us of spiritual life, which is sanctifying grace, and brings everlasting death and damnation on the soul.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 282. How many things are necessary to make a sin mortal? </p> 
 <p>A. To make a sin mortal, three things are necessary:</p>  
 <p>   1.a grievous matter, sufficient reflection, and full consent of the will.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 283. What do we mean by "grievous matter" with regard to sin? </p> 
 <p>A. By "grievous matter" with regard to sin we mean that the thought, word or deed by which mortal sin is</p> 
 <p>committed must be either very bad in itself or severely prohibited, and therefore sufficient to make a mortal sin if</p> 
 <p>we deliberately yield to it.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 284. What does "sufficient reflection and full consent of the will" mean? </p> 
 <p>A. "Sufficient reflection" means that we must know the thought, word or deed to be sinful at the time we are guilty of it; and "full consent of the will" means that we must fully and willfully yield to it.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 285. What are sins committed without reflection or consent called? </p> 
 <p>A. Sins committed without reflection or consent are called material sins; that is, they would be formal or real sins if we knew their sinfulness at the time we committed them. Thus to eat flesh meat on a day of abstinence without</p> 
 <p>knowing it to be a day of abstinence or without thinking of the prohibition, would be a material sin.</p>  <b>
 </b><p>Q. 286. Do past material sins become real sins as soon as we discover their sinfulness? </p> 
 <p>A. Past material sins do not become real sins as soon as we discover their sinfulness, unless we again repeat them</p> 
 <p>with full knowledge and consent.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 287. How can we know what sins are considered mortal? </p> 
 <p>A. We can know what sins are considered mortal from Holy Scripture; from the teaching of the Church, and from</p> 
 <p>the writings of the Fathers and Doctors of the Church.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 288. Why is it wrong to judge others guilty of sin? </p> 
 <p>A. It is wrong to judge others guilty of sin because we cannot know for certain that their sinful act was committed</p> 
 <p>with sufficient reflection and full consent of the will.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 289. What sin does he commit who without sufficient reason believes another guilty of sin? </p> 
 <p>A. He who without sufficient reason believes another guilty of sin commits a sin of rash judgment.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 290. What is venial sin? </p> 
 <p>A. Venial sin is a slight offense against the law of God in matters of less importance, or in matters of great</p> 
 <p>importance it is an offense committed without sufficient reflection or full consent of the will.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 291. Can we always distinguish venial from mortal sin? </p> 
 <p>A. We cannot always distinguish venial from mortal sin, and in such cases we must leave the decision to our</p> 
 <p>confessor.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 292. Can slight offenses ever become mortal sins? </p> 
 <p>A. Slight offenses can become mortal sins if we commit them through defiant contempt for God or His law; and</p> 
 <p>also when they are followed by very evil consequences, which we foresee in committing them.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 293. Which are the effects of venial sin? </p> 
 <p>A. The effects of venial sin are the lessening of the love of God in our heart, the making us less worthy of His help,  	and the weakening of the power to resist mortal sin.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 294. How can we know a thought, word or deed to be sinful? </p> 
 <p>A. We can know a thought, word or deed to be sinful if it, or the neglect of it, is forbidden by any law of God or of His Church, or if it is opposed to any supernatural virtue.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 295. Which are the chief sources of sin? </p> 
 <p>A. The chief sources of sin are seven:</p>  
 <p>   1.Pride, Covetousness, Lust, Anger, Gluttony, Envy, and Sloth,</p>  
 <p>and they are commonly called capital sins.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 296. What is pride? </p> 
 <p>A. Pride is an excessive love of our own ability; so that we would rather sinfully disobey than humble ourselves.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 297. What effect has pride on our souls? </p> 
 <p>A. Pride begets in our souls sinful ambition, vainglory, presumption and hypocrisy.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 298. What is covetousness? </p> 
 <p>A. Covetousness is an excessive desire for worldly things.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 299. What effect has covetousness on our souls? </p> 
 <p>A. Covetousness begets in our souls unkindness, dishonesty, deceit and want of charity.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 300. What is lust? </p> 
 <p>A. Lust is an excessive desire for the sinful pleasures forbidden by the Sixth Commandment.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 301. What effect has lust on our souls? </p> 
 <p>A. Lust begets in our souls a distaste for holy things, a perverted conscience, a hatred for God, and it very</p> 
 <p>frequently leads to a complete loss of faith.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 302. What is anger? </p> 
 <p>A. Anger is an excessive emotion of the mind excited against any person or thing, or it is an excessive desire for</p> 
 <p>revenge.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 303. What effect has anger on our soul? </p> 
 <p>A. Anger begets in our souls impatience, hatred, irreverence, and too often the habit of cursing.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 304. What is gluttony? </p> 
 <p>A. Gluttony is an excessive desire for food or drink.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 305. What kind of a sin is drunkenness? </p> 
 <p>A. Drunkenness is a sin of gluttony by which a person deprives himself of the use of his reason by the excessive</p> 
 <p>taking of intoxicating drink.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 306. Is drunkenness always a mortal sin? </p> 
 <p>A. Deliberate drunkenness is always a mortal sin if the person be completely deprived of the use of reason by it,</p> 
 <p>but drunkenness that is not intended or desired may be excused from mortal sin.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 307. What are the chief effects of habitual drunkenness? </p> 
 <p>A. Habitual drunkenness injures the body, weakens the mind, leads its victim into many vices and exposes him to</p> 
 <p>the danger of dying in a state of mortal sin.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 308. What three sins seem to cause most evil in the world? </p> 
 <p>A. Drunkenness, dishonesty and impurity seem to cause most evil in the world, and they are therefore to be</p> 
 <p>carefully avoided at all times.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 309. What is envy? </p> 
 <p>A. Envy is a feeling of sorrow at another's good fortune and joy at the evil which befalls him; as if we ourselves</p> 
 <p>were injured by the good and benefited by the evil that comes to him.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 310. What effect has envy on the soul? </p> 
 <p>A. Envy begets in the soul a want of charity for our neighbor and produces a spirit of detraction, back-biting and</p> 
 <p>slander.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 311. What is sloth? </p> 
 <p>A. Sloth is a laziness of the mind and body, through which we neglect our duties on account of the labor they</p> 
 <p>require.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 312. What effect has sloth upon the soul? </p> 
 <p>A. Sloth begets in the soul a spirit of indifference in our spiritual duties and a disgust for prayer.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 313. Why are the seven sources of sin called capital sins? </p> 
 <p>A. The seven sources of sin are called capital sins because they rule over our other sins and are the causes of them.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 314. What do we mean by our predominant sin or ruling passion? </p> 
 <p>A. By our predominant sin, or ruling passion, we mean the sin into which we fall most frequently and which we find it hardest to resist.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 315. How can we best overcome our sins? </p> 
 <p>A. We can best overcome our sins by guarding against our predominant or ruling sin.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 316. Should we give up trying to be good when we seem not to succeed in overcoming our faults? </p> 
 <p>A. We should not give up trying to be good when we seem not to succeed in overcoming our faults, because our</p> 
 <p>efforts to be good will keep us from becoming worse than we are.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 317. What virtues are opposed to the seven capital sins? </p> 
 <p>A. Humility is opposed to pride; generosity to covetousness; chastity to lust; meekness to anger; temperance to</p> 
 <p>gluttony; brotherly love to envy, and diligence to sloth.</p>  
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> 
 <p>LESSON SEVENTH: On the Incarnation and Redemption </p>  <b>
 </b><p>Q. 318. What does "incarnation" mean, and what does "redemption" mean? </p> 
 <p>A. "Incarnation" means the act of clothing with flesh. Thus Our Lord clothed His divinity with a human body.</p> 
 <p>"Redemption" means to buy back again.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 319. Did God abandon man after he fell into sin? </p> 
 <p>A. God did not abandon man after he fell into sin, but promised him a Redeemer, who was to satisfy for man's sin</p> 
 <p>and reopen to him the gates of heaven.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 320. What do we mean by the "gates of heaven"? </p> 
 <p>A. By the "gates of heaven" we mean the divine power by which God keeps us out of heaven or admits us into it,</p> 
 <p>at His pleasure.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 321. Who is the Redeemer? </p> 
 <p>A. Our Blessed Lord and Saviour Jesus Christ is the Redeemer of mankind.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 322. What does the name "Jesus" signify and how was this name given to Our Lord? </p> 
 <p>A. The name "Jesus" signifies Saviour or Redeemer, and this name was given to Our Lord by an Angel who</p> 
 <p>appeared to Joseph and said: "Mary shall bring forth a Son; and thou shalt call His name Jesus."</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 323. What does the name "Christ" signify? </p> 
 <p>A. The name "Christ" means the same as Messias, and signifies Anointed; because, as in the Old Law, Prophets,</p> 
 <p>High Priests and Kings were anointed with oil; so Jesus, the Great Prophet, High Priest and King of the New Law, was anointed as man with the fullness of divine power.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 324. How did Christ show and prove His divine power? </p> 
 <p>A. Christ showed and proved His divine power chiefly by His miracles, which are extraordinary works that can be</p> 
 <p>performed only by power received from God, and which have, therefore, His sanction and authority.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 325. What, then, did the miracles of Jesus Christ prove? </p> 
 <p>A. The miracles of Jesus Christ proved that whatever He said was true, and that when He declared Himself to be</p> 
 <p>the Son of God He really was what He claimed to be.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 326. Could not men have been deceived in the miracles of Christ? </p> 
 <p>A. Men could not have been deceived in the miracles of Christ because they were performed in the most open</p> 
 <p>manner and usually in the presence of great multitudes of people, among whom were many of Christ's enemies,</p> 
 <p>ever ready to expose any deceit. And if Christ performed no real miracles, how, then, could He have converted</p> 
 <p>the world and have persuaded sinful men to give up what they loved and do the difficult things that the Christian</p> 
 <p>religion imposes?</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 327. Could not false accounts of these miracles have been written after the death of Our Lord? </p> 
 <p>A. False accounts of these miracles could not have been written after the death of Our Lord; for then neither His</p> 
 <p>friends nor His enemies would have believed them without proof. Moreover, the enemies of Christ did not deny the miracles, but tried to explain them by attributing them to the power of the devil or other causes. Again, the</p> 
 <p>Apostles and the Evangelists who wrote the accounts suffered death to testify their belief in the words and works</p> 
 <p>of Our Lord.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 328. Did Jesus Christ die to redeem all men of every age and race without exception? </p> 
 <p>A. Jesus Christ died to redeem all men of every age and race without exception; and every person born into the</p> 
 <p>world should share in His merits, without which no one can be saved.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 329. How are the merits of Jesus Christ applied to our souls? </p> 
 <p>A. The merits of Jesus Christ are applied to our souls through the Sacraments, and especially through Baptism and Penance, which restore us to the friendship of God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 330. What do you believe of Jesus Christ? </p> 
 <p>A. I believe that Jesus Christ is the Son of God, the second Person of the Blessed Trinity, true God and true man.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 331. Cannot we also be called the Children of God, and therefore His sons and daughters? </p> 
 <p>A. We can be called the Children of God because He has adopted us by His grace or because He is the Father</p> 
 <p>who has created us; but we are not, therefore, His real Children; whereas, Jesus Christ, His only real and true Son,</p> 
 <p>was neither adopted nor created, but was begotten of His Father from all eternity.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 332. Why is Jesus Christ true God? </p> 
 <p>A. Jesus Christ is true God because He is the true and only Son of God the Father.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 333. Why is Jesus Christ true man? </p> 
 <p>A. Jesus Christ is true man because He is the Son of the Blessed Virgin Mary and has a body and soul like ours.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 334. Who was the foster father or guardian of Our Lord while on earth? </p> 
 <p>A. St. Joseph, the husband of the Blessed Virgin, was the foster-father or guardian of Our Lord while on earth.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 335. Is Jesus Christ in heaven as God or as man? </p> 
 <p>A. Since His Ascension Jesus Christ is in heaven both as God and as man.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 336. How many natures are there in Jesus Christ? </p> 
 <p>A. In Jesus Christ there are two natures, the nature of God and the nature of man.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 337. Is Jesus Christ more than one person? </p> 
 <p>A. No. Jesus Christ is but one Divine Person.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 338. From what do we learn that Jesus Christ is but one person? </p> 
 <p>A. We learn that Jesus Christ is but one person from Holy Scripture and from the constant teaching of the Church,</p> 
 <p>which has condemned all those who teach the contrary.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 339. Was Jesus Christ always God? </p> 
 <p>A. Jesus Christ was always God, as He is the second person of the Blessed Trinity, equal to His Father from all</p> 
 <p>eternity.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 340. Was Jesus Christ always man? </p> 
 <p>A. Jesus Christ was not always man, but became man at the time of His Incarnation.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 341. What do you mean by the Incarnation? </p> 
 <p>A. By the Incarnation I mean that the Son of God was made man.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 342. How was the Son of God made man? </p> 
 <p>A. The Son of God was conceived and made man by the power of the Holy Ghost, in the womb of the Blessed</p> 
 <p>Virgin Mary.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 343. Is the Blessed Virgin Mary truly the Mother of God? </p> 
 <p>A. The Blessed Virgin Mary is truly the Mother of God, because the same Divine Person who is the Son of God is</p> 
 <p>also the Son of the Blessed Virgin Mary.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 344. Did the Son of God become man immediately after the sin of our first parents? </p> 
 <p>A. The Son of God did not become man immediately after the sin of our first parents, but was promised to them as a Redeemer.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 345. How many years passed from the time Adam sinned till the time the Redeemer came? </p> 
 <p>A. About 4,000 years passed from the time Adam sinned till the time the Redeemer came.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 346. What was the moral condition of the world just before the coming of Our Lord? </p> 
 <p>A. Just before the coming of Our Lord the moral condition of the world was very bad. Idolatry, injustice, cruelty,</p> 
 <p>immorality and horrid vices were common almost everywhere.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 347. Why was the coming of the Redeemer so long delayed? </p> 
 <p>A. The coming of the Redeemer was so long delayed that the world -- suffering from every misery -- might learn</p> 
 <p>the great evil of sin and know that God alone could help fallen man.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 348. When was the Redeemer promised to mankind? </p> 
 <p>A. The Redeemer was first promised to mankind in the Garden of Paradise, and often afterward through Abraham</p> 
 <p>and his descendants, the patriarchs, and through numerous prophets.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 349. Who were the prophets? </p> 
 <p>A. The prophets were inspired men to whom God revealed the future, that they might with absolute certainty make it known to the people.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 350. What did the prophets foretell concerning the Redeemer? </p> 
 <p>A. The prophets, taken together, foretold so accurately all the circumstances of the birth, life, death, resurrection</p> 
 <p>and glory of the Redeemer that no one who carefully studied their writings could fail to recognize Him when He came.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 351. Have all these prophecies concerning the Redeemer been fulfilled? </p> 
 <p>A. All the prophecies concerning the Redeemer have been fulfilled in every point by the circumstances of Christ's</p> 
 <p>birth, life, death, resurrection and glory; and He is, therefore, the Redeemer promised to mankind from the time of</p> 
 <p>Adam.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 352. Where shall we find these prophecies concerning the Redeemer? </p> 
 <p>A. We shall find these prophecies concerning the Redeemer in the prophetic books of the Bible or Holy Scripture.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 353. If the Redeemer's coming was so clearly foretold, why did not all recognize Him when He came? </p> 
 <p>A. All did not recognize the Redeemer when He came, because many knew only part of the prophecies; and</p> 
 <p>taking those concerning His glory and omitting those concerning His suffering, they could not understand His life.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 354. How could they be saved who lived before the Son of God became man? </p> 
 <p>A. They who lived before the Son of God became man could be saved by believing in a Redeemer to come, and</p> 
 <p>by keeping the Commandments.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 355. On what day was the Son of God conceived and made man? </p> 
 <p>A. The Son of God was conceived and made man on Annunciation Day -- the day on which the Angel Gabriel</p> 
 <p>announced to the Blessed Virgin Mary that she was to be the Mother of God.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 356. On what day was Christ born? </p> 
 <p>A. Christ was born on Christmas Day, in a stable at Bethlehem, over nineteen hundred years ago.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 357. Why did the Blessed Virgin and St. Joseph go to Bethlehem just before the birth of Our Lord? </p> 
 <p>A. The Blessed Virgin and St. Joseph went to Bethlehem in obedience to the Roman Emperor, who ordered all his</p> 
 <p>subjects to register their names in the towns or cities of their ancestors. Bethlehem was the City of David, the royal ancestor of Mary and Joseph, hence they had to register there. All this was done by the Will of God, that the</p> 
 <p>prophecies concerning the birth of His Divine Son might be fulfilled.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 358. Why was Christ born in a stable? </p> 
 <p>A. Christ was born in a stable because Joseph and Mary were poor and strangers in Bethlehem, and without</p> 
 <p>money they could find no other shelter. This was permitted by Our Lord that we might learn a lesson from His</p> 
 <p>great humility.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 359. In giving the ancestors or forefathers of Our Lord, why do the Gospels give the ancestors of</p> 
 <p>Joseph, who was only Christ's foster-father, and not the ancestors of Mary, who was Christ's real parent? </p> 
 <p>A. In giving the ancestors of Our Lord, the Gospels give the ancestors of Joseph:</p>  
 <p>   1.(1) Because the ancestors of women were not usually recorded by the Jews; and </p> 
 <p>   2.(2) Because Mary and Joseph were members of the same tribe, and had, therefore, the same ancestors; so</p> 
 <p>     that, in giving the ancestors of Joseph, the Gospels give also those of Mary; and this was understood by</p> 
 <p>     those for whom the Gospels were intended.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 360. Had Our Lord any brothers or sisters ? </p> 
 <p>A. Our Lord had no brothers or sisters. When the Gospels speak of His brethren they mean only His near</p> 
 <p>relations. His Blessed Mother Mary was always a Virgin as well before and at His birth as after it.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 361. Who were among the first to adore the Infant Jesus? </p> 
 <p>A. The shepherds of Bethlehem, to whom His birth was announced by Angels; and the Magi or three wise men,</p> 
 <p>who were guided to His crib by a miraculous star, were among the first to adore the Infant Jesus. We recall the</p> 
 <p>adoration of the Magi on the feast of the Epiphany, which means appearance or manifestation, namely, of Our</p> 
 <p>Saviour.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 362. Who sought to kill the Infant Jesus? </p> 
 <p>A. Herod sought to kill the Infant Jesus because he thought the influence of Christ -- the new-born King -- would</p> 
 <p>deprive him of his throne.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 363. How was the Holy Infant rescued from the power of Herod? </p> 
 <p>A. The Holy Infant was rescued from the power of Herod by the flight into Egypt, when St. Joseph -- warned by</p> 
 <p>an Angel -- fled hastily into that country with Jesus and Mary.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 364. How did Herod hope to accomplish his wicked designs? </p> 
 <p>A. Herod hoped to accomplish his wicked designs by murdering all the infants in and near Bethlehem. The day on</p> 
 <p>which we commemorate the death of these first little martyrs, who shed their blood for Christ's sake, is called the</p> 
 <p>feast of Holy Innocents.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 365. How may the years of Christ's life be divided? </p> 
 <p>A. The years of Christ's life may be divided into three parts:</p>  
 <p>   1.(1) His childhood, extending from His birth to His twelfth year, when He went with his parents to worship in</p> 
 <p>     the Temple of Jerusalem. </p> 
 <p>   2.(2) His hidden life, which extends from His twelfth to His thirtieth year, during which time He dwelt with His</p> 
 <p>     parents at Nazareth. </p> 
 <p>   3.(3) His public life, extending from His thirtieth year -- or from His baptism by St. John the Baptist to His</p> 
 <p>     death; during which time He taught His doctrines and established His Church.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 366. Why is Christ's life thus divided? </p> 
 <p>A. Christ's life is thus divided to show that all classes find in Him their model. In childhood He gave an example to the young; in His hidden life an example to those who consecrate themselves to the service of God in a religious state; and in His public life an example to all Christians without exception.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 367. How long did Christ live on earth? </p> 
 <p>A. Christ lived on earth about thirty-three years, and led a most holy life in poverty and suffering.</p>  
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 368. Why did Christ live so long on earth? </p> 
 <p>A. Christ lived so long on earth to show us the way to heaven by His teachings and example.</p>  
 <p> </p> 
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>LESSON EIGHTH: On Our Lord's Passion, Death, Resurrection, and Ascension </p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 369. What do we mean by Our Lord's Passion? </p> 
 <p>A. By Our Lord's Passion we mean His dreadful sufferings from His agony in the garden till the moment of His</p> 
 <p>death.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 370. What did Jesus Christ suffer? </p> 
 <p>A. Jesus Christ suffered a bloody sweat, a cruel scourging, was crowned with thorns, and was crucified.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 371. When did Our Lord suffer the "bloody sweat"? </p> 
 <p>A. Our Lord suffered the "bloody sweat" while drops of blood came forth from every pore of His body, during His agony in the Garden of Olives, near Jerusalem, where He went to pray on the night His Passion began.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 372. Who accompanied Our Lord to the Garden of Olives on the night of His Agony? </p> 
 <p>A. The Apostles Peter, James and John, the same who had witnessed His transfiguration on the mount,</p> 
 <p>accompanied Our Lord to the Garden of Olives, to watch and pray with Him on the night of His agony.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 373. What do we mean by the transfiguration of Our Lord? </p> 
 <p>A. By the transfiguration of Our Lord we mean the supernatural change in His appearance when He showed</p> 
 <p>Himself to His Apostles in great glory and brilliancy in which "His face did shine as the sun and His garments</p> 
 <p>became white as snow."</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 374. Who were present at the transfiguration? </p> 
 <p>A. There were present at the transfiguration -- besides the Apostles Peter, James and John, who witnessed it --</p> 
 <p>the two great and holy men of the Old Law, Moses and Elias, talking with Our Lord.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 375. What caused Our Lord's agony in the garden? </p> 
 <p>A It is believed Our Lord's agony in the garden was caused:</p>  
 <p>   1.(1) By his clear knowledge of all He was soon to endure; </p> 
 <p>   2.(2) By the sight of the many offenses committed against His Father by the sins of the whole world; </p> 
 <p>   3.(3) By His knowledge of men's ingratitude for the blessings of redemption.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 376. Why was Christ cruelly scourged? </p> 
 <p>A. Christ was cruelly scourged by Pilate's orders, that the sight of His bleeding body might move His enemies to</p> 
 <p>spare His life.</p>  <b>
 </b><p> </p> 
 <p>Q. 377. Why was Christ crowned with thorns? </p> 
 <p>A. Christ was crowned with thorns in mockery because He had said He was a King.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 378. Could Christ, if He pleased, have escaped the tortures of His Passion? </p> 
 <p>A. Christ could, if He pleased, have escaped the tortures of His Passion, because He foresaw them and had it in</p> 
 <p>His power to overcome His enemies.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 379. Was it necessary for Christ to suffer so much in order to redeem us? </p> 
 <p>A. It was not necessary for Christ to suffer so much in order to redeem us, for the least of His sufferings was more</p> 
 <p>than sufficient to atone for all the sins of mankind. By suffering so much He showed His great love for us.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 380. Who betrayed Our Lord? </p> 
 <p>A. Judas, one of His Apostles, betrayed Our Lord, and from His sin we may learn that even the good may become</p> 
 <p>very wicked by the abuse of their free will.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 381. How was Christ condemned to death? </p> 
 <p>A. Through the influence of those who hated Him, Christ was condemned to death, after an unjust trial, at which</p> 
 <p>false witnesses were induced to testify against Him.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 382. On what day did Christ die? </p> 
 <p>A. Christ died on Good Friday.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 383. Why do you call that day "good" on which Christ died so sorrowful a death? </p> 
 <p>A. We call that day good on which Christ died because by His death He showed His great love for man, and</p> 
 <p>purchased for him every blessing.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 384. How long was Our Lord hanging on the cross before He died? </p> 
 <p>A. Our Lord was hanging on the Cross about three hours before He died. While thus suffering, His enemies stood</p> 
 <p>around blaspheming and mocking Him. By His death He proved Himself a real mortal man, for He could not die in His divine nature.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 385. What do we call the words Christ spoke while hanging on the Cross? </p> 
 <p>A. We call the words Christ spoke while hanging on the Cross "the seven last words of Jesus on the Cross." They</p> 
 <p>teach us the dispositions we should have at the hour of death.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 386. Repeat the seven last words or sayings of Jesus on the Cross. </p> 
 <p>A. The seven last words or sayings of Jesus on the Cross are:</p>  
 <p>   1.(1) "Father, forgive them, for they know not what they do," in which He forgives and prays for His enemies. </p> 
 <p>   2.(2) "Amen, I say to thee, this day thou shalt be with Me in Paradise," in which He pardons the penitent</p> 
 <p>     sinner. </p> 
 <p>   3.(3) "Woman, behold thy Son" -- "Behold thy Mother," in which He gave up what was dearest to Him on</p> 
 <p>     earth, and gave us Mary for our Mother. </p> 
 <p>   4.(4) "My God, my God, why hast Thou forsaken Me?" from which we learn the suffering of His mind. </p> 
 <p>   5.(5) "I thirst," from which we learn the suffering of His body. </p> 
 <p>   6.(6) "All is consummated," by which He showed the fulfillment of all the prophecies concerning Him and the</p> 
 <p>     completion of the work of our redemption. </p> 
 <p>   7.(7) "Father, into Thy hands I commend my spirit," by which He showed His perfect resignation to the Will of</p> 
 <p>     His Eternal Father.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 387. What happened at the death of Our Lord? </p> 
 <p>A. At the death of Our Lord there were darkness and earthquake; many holy dead came forth from their graves,</p> 
 <p>and the veil concealing the Holy of Holies, in the Temple of Jerusalem, was torn asunder.</p>  
 <p><br> <b>Q. 388. What was the Holy of Holies in the temple? </b></p> 
 <p>A. The Holy of Holies was the sacred part of the Temple, in which the Ark of the Covenant was kept, and where</p> 
 <p>the high priest consulted the Will of God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 389. What was the "Ark of the Covenant"? </p> 
 <p>A. The Ark of the Covenant was a precious box in which were kept the tablets of stone bearing the written</p> 
 <p>Commandments of God, the rod which Aaron changed into a serpent before King Pharao, and a portion of the</p> 
 <p>manna with which the Israelites were miraculously fed in the desert. The Ark of the Covenant was a figure of the</p> 
 <p>Tabernacle in which we keep the Holy Eucharist.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 390. Why was the veil of the Temple torn asunder at the death of Christ? </p> 
 <p>A. The veil of the Temple was torn asunder at the death of Christ because at His death the Jewish religion ceased</p> 
 <p>to be the true religion, and God no longer manifested His presence in the Temple.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 391. Why did the Jewish religion, which up to the death of Christ had been the true religion, cease at</p> 
 <p>that time to be the true religion? </p> 
 <p>A. The Jewish religion, which, up to the death of Christ, had been the true religion, ceased at that time to be the</p> 
 <p>true religion, because it was only a promise of the redemption and figure of the Christian religion, and when the</p> 
 <p>redemption was accomplished and the Christian religion established by the death of Christ, the promise and the</p> 
 <p>figure were no longer necessary.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 392. Were all the laws of the Jewish religion abolished by the establishment of Christianity? </p> 
 <p>A. The moral laws of the Jewish religion were not abolished by the establishment of Christianity, for Christ came</p> 
 <p>not to destroy these laws, but to make them more perfect. Its ceremonial laws were abolished when the Temple of</p> 
 <p>Jerusalem ceased to be the House of God.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 393. What do we mean by moral and ceremonial laws? </p> 
 <p>A. By "moral" laws we mean laws regarding good and evil. By "ceremonial" laws we mean laws regulating the</p> 
 <p>manner of worshipping God in Temple or Church.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 394. Where did Christ die? </p> 
 <p>A. Christ died on Mount Calvary.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 395. Where was Mount Calvary, and what does the name signify? </p> 
 <p>A. Mount Calvary was the place of execution, not far from Jerusalem; and the name signifies the "place of skulls."</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 396. How did Christ die? </p> 
 <p>A. Christ was nailed to the Cross, and died on it between two thieves.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 397. Why was Our Lord crucified between thieves? </p> 
 <p>A. Our Lord was crucified between thieves that His enemies might thus add to His disgrace by making Him equal</p> 
 <p>to the worst criminals.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 398. Why did Christ suffer and die? </p> 
 <p>A. Christ suffered and died for our sins.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 399. How was Our Lord's body buried? </p> 
 <p>A. Our Lord's body was wrapped in a clean linen cloth and laid in a new sepulchre or tomb cut in a rock, by</p> 
 <p>Joseph of Arimathea and other pious persons who believed in Our Divine Lord.</p>  
 <p> </p> <b>
 </b><p>Q. 400. What lessons do we learn from the sufferings and death of Christ? </p> 
 <p>A. From the sufferings and death of Christ we learn the great evil of sin, the hatred God bears to it, and the</p>
